## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials constitutive modeling (thermo-mechanical behavior)
**Analysis**: The variables map directly to a constitutive relation for a solid: stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) with explicit temperature (T) dependence. Common models include thermoelasticity, temperature-dependent elastic modulus, and temperature-softening plasticity/flow-stress laws.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness changes approximately linearly with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (inverse shift): sigma = c0 * epsilon / (T + c1) (stiffness decreases with increasing temperature over a range)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate strain nonlinear elasticity)
- Exponential strain-stiffening: sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - c2) (rubber-like or phenomenological stiffening response)
- Hyperelastic-type (log form): sigma = c0 * log(c1 * epsilon + c2) (compressible phenomenological elasticity; small-strain log expansion possible)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening over a range)
- Ludwik-type hardening with offset: sigma = c0 + c1 * (epsilon + c2)**c3 (yield stress plus strain hardening; avoids singularity at epsilon=0)
- Ramberg–Osgood (implicit compliance form): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 (elastic + nonlinear/plastic compliance; often inverted numerically to sigma(epsilon,T))
- Thermal softening factor (multiplicative): sigma = (c0 * epsilon**c1) * exp(c2 * T) (temperature-accelerated weakening/strengthening over limited range; sign of c2 determines trend)
- Thermal softening (rational): sigma = (c0 * epsilon**c1) / (c2 * T + c3) (flow stress reduced by increasing temperature)
- Coupled polynomial (interaction term): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T + c2 * epsilon * T (thermo-mechanical coupling over a limited operating window)
- Yield-like saturation with strain (tanh): sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (stress approaches a plateau with strain; temperature scales the plateau)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain linear elasticity → sigma proportional to epsilon; temperature dependence often enters through a T-dependent prefactor multiplying epsilon (effective modulus E(T)).
- Thermal softening of strength/modulus → multiplicative factors that decrease with T (e.g., exp(c*T) with negative c, or division by (c*T+c0)).
- Strain hardening in plasticity → sigma increasing sublinearly/superlinearly with epsilon via epsilon**n or (epsilon+c0)**n; n controls curvature.
- Yield/plateau behavior with increasing strain → bounded functions such as tanh(c*epsilon) or rational forms that approach a finite limit as epsilon grows.
- Elastic-to-plastic transition (rounded knee) → additive combination of a linear term in epsilon plus a nonlinear term (e.g., c*epsilon + c*(epsilon+c0)**n).
- Thermo-mechanical coupling beyond separable effects → interaction terms like epsilon*T or (epsilon**n)*(T-dependent factor) indicating sensitivity of hardening to temperature.
- Avoid singular behavior near epsilon=0 → use shifted strain (epsilon + c0) inside powers/logs to model initial yielding/offset strains robustly.
- Data spanning wide temperature ranges often favors normalized/shifted temperature arguments → functions of (T + c0) rather than bare T to prevent divergences and capture reference-temperature behavior.

- Term 3: `3.554*T*log(epsilon+1) - 1178.9*log(epsilon+1)` (T*log and log terms)

So GT = `64.95*epsilon^0.614*exp(-4.443/T) - 0.2148*T + 71.26 + 3.554*T*log(epsilon+1) - 1178.9*log(epsilon+1)`

Key structural features of GT:
1. **epsilon^c (fractional power)** multiplied by **exp(-c/T)** (Arrhenius)
2. **Linear in T**
3. **T*log(epsilon+1)** - product of T and log(epsilon+1)

- log(epsilon+1) dependence
